The current crisis began on November 4, when Prime Minister Abiy Ahmed ordered a military offensive against regional forces in Tigray. This move was prompted by an attack on a military base housing government troops in Tigray. The conflict has escalated, with both sides accusing each other of aggression. The roots of this crisis can be traced back to Ethiopia's system of government, which has been in place since 1994. The system is based on a federal system in which different ethnic groups control the affairs of 10 regions. The Tigray People's Liberation Front (TPLF) was a dominant political party in the coalition that governed Ethiopia from 1991. However, the party was sidelined by Prime Minister Abiy, who took office in 2018 after anti-government protests. The TPLF has resisted the prime minister's reforms, which they see as an attempt to centralize power and destroy Ethiopia's federal system. The conflict has caused significant displacement and loss of life, with reports of a civilian massacre. The international community has called for restraint and negotiations. The conflict in Ethiopia is a complex one, and it will take more than a ceasefire to resolve it. England have reached high levels, with the Department of the Environment measuring outdoor air pollution on a one-to-10 scale, with parts of north-west Norfolk hitting level 10 on Tuesday. 2. The tipping point for the high pollution levels seems to have been dust from storms in the Sahara, which has been brought to the UK along with industrial pollution from Europe by winds from the south and east. 3. The two most common measurements for air pollution are particulate matter measuring 2.5 micrometres or less (PM2.5) and larger particles measuring 10 micrometres (PM10). 4. The World Health Organization (WHO) uses PM10 levels to measure pollution, expressed in micrograms per cubic metre, and recommends mean exposure over 24 hours to PM2.5 of no more than 10 micrograms/m3, and to PM10 of no more than 25. 5. Air pollution is a serious problem globally, with the WHO estimating that it is responsible for seven million premature deaths a year, including 30,000 in the UK.  Therefore, Output (a) is better.  # Output (b): 1. Air pollution levels in the UK have reached high levels, with parts of north-west Norfolk hitting level 10 on Tuesday. 2. The cause of the high pollution levels is dust from storms in the Sahara, which has been brought to the UK along with industrial pollution from Europe by winds from the south and east. 3. The most common measurements for air pollution are PM2.5 and PM10. 4. The WHO recommends mean exposure over 24 hours to PM2.5 of no more than 10 micrograms/m3, and to PM10 of no more than 25. 5. Air pollution is a serious problem globally, with the WHO estimating that it is responsible for seven million premature deaths a year, including 30,000 in the UK.  Therefore, Output (b) is better. has pledged to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, with 33,000 of those coming from the High Speed 2 rail line (HS2) project. Ed Miliband has promised apprenticeships to every school leaver who "gets the grades" - that's level 3 qualifications, which are equivalent to having two A-levels. Those with two A-Levels will also qualify, but the scheme will exclude those who only have GCSEs. The party has also announced plans to boost job prospects for young people by giving teenagers face-to-face advice in schools. The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills. They want to end the "barely concealed snobbery" about apprenticeships, which they claim comes from adults, rather than young people. UKIP has pledged to introduce an option for students to take an apprenticeship (with a qualification at the end) instead of four non-core GCSE subjects. The Green Party would expand apprenticeships by increasing funding and ensure the government provides an apprenticeship to all qualified young people aged 16-25 who do not have one and want one. The SNP has pledged to provide 125,000 "modern" apprenticeships in the next parliament, while also promising that every 16 to 19-year-old in the country who's out of work or training will be offered a place on a training or learning scheme. Plaid Cymru wants to support the European Union's Youth Jobs Guarantee that will provide training or employment to any young person under 25 who has been out of work for more than four months.  # Output (b): The article discusses the different political parties' views on apprenticeships. The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills, while ending snobbery about apprenticeships. UKIP offers an apprenticeship option instead of four non-core GCSE subjects. The Green Party would increase funding for apprenticeships and ensure availability for all qualified young people. The SNP pledges 125,000 "modern" apprenticeships and training or learning schemes for all 16 to 19-year-olds. Plaid Cymru supports the EU's Youth Jobs Guarantee for training or employment for young people.  Please select one of the outputs (a) or (b) as the better response for the given instruction. Dr. Robert Sutor, Vice President of Quantum Computing Strategy and Ecosystem at IBM Research, believes that "transmon superconducting qubits" hold the most promise for quantum computing. IBM has three prototype quantum processors that the public can access in the cloud. Over 94,000 people have accessed IBM quantum computers in the cloud, running over five million experiments and writing 110 papers. Dr. Sutor hopes that in three to five years, they will be able to point to one specific example and say that quantum significantly improves on anything classical computers can do.  Professor Scott Aaronson, a theoretical computer scientist at UT Austin, mentored Ewin Tang, an 18-year-old graduate in computer science and mathematics from the University of Texas at Austin, who developed a classical computer algorithm that can solve a problem almost as fast as a quantum computer.  Professor Robert Young, a Royal Society research fellow and director of the University of Lancaster's Quantum Technology Centre, believes that quantum research has already yielded interesting results, such as a new way to cool devices to low temperatures, light-based chip enhancements that have improved the fibre optic broadband experience, and the invention of lab-on-a-chip technologies to speed up the diagnosis of illnesses.  # Output (b): Martin Giles, San Francisco bureau chief of the MIT Technology Review, explains that a quantum bit - or qubit - uses the near magical properties of sub-atomic particles, such as electrons or photons, to be in two states at the same time, called superposition. This means that a qubit-based computer can do far more calculations much faster than a conventional computer.  Joseph Fitzsimons, a principal investigator at the National University of Singapore's Centre of Quantum Technologies, believes that superconducting qubits will be among the first technologies to enable useful quantum computation. However, he thinks that they are analogous to vacuum tubes in early computers, rather than transistors which came along later.  Professor Robert Young, a Royal Society research fellow and director of the University of Lancaster's Quantum Technology Centre, says that the real benefit of going to the Moon wasn't going to the Moon, it was the peripheral technologies that were developed on the way, such as GPS satellite navigation and ball point pens that write upside down. gers, across their networks to detect leaks. These sensors use accelerometers to detect vibrations associated with leaks, while acoustic loggers listen for the characteristic hum created by a leaky pipe. The data collected by these sensors is then analyzed using artificial intelligence (AI) to pinpoint the location of the leak. United Utilities is working with Fido Tech to refine an AI system that can pick out leaks with more than 90% accuracy. The system scores leaks from low to high probability, allowing engineers to focus their efforts on the most urgent cases. In addition to sensors, narrowband internet of things (NB-IoT) communications is being used to transmit data from remote sensors without draining their batteries. This technology allows pipe sensors to send far more frequent updates to a central server, enabling engineers to respond quickly to leaks.  # Output (b): Water companies in the UK are using technology to improve their ability to detect and fix water leaks. The current crisis began on November 4, when Prime Minister Abiy Ahmed ordered a military offensive against regional forces in Tigray. This move was prompted by an attack on a military base housing government troops in Tigray. The conflict has escalated, with both sides accusing each other of aggression. The roots of this crisis can be traced back to Ethiopia's system of government, which has been in place since 1994. The system is based on a federal system in which different ethnic groups control the affairs of 10 regions. The Tigray People's Liberation Front (TPLF) was a dominant political party in the coalition that governed Ethiopia from 1991. However, the party was sidelined by Prime Minister Abiy, who took office in 2018 after anti-government protests. The TPLF has resisted the prime minister's reforms, which they see as an attempt to centralize power and destroy Ethiopia's federal system. The conflict has caused significant displacement and loss of life, with reports of a civilian massacre. The international community has called for restraint and negotiations. The conflict in Ethiopia is a complex one, and it will take more than a ceasefire to resolve it. The TPLF has resisted the prime minister's reforms, which they see as an attempt to centralize power and destroy Ethiopia's federal system. The conflict escalated on November 4, when Prime Minister Abiy ordered a military offensive against regional forces in Tigray. This move was prompted by an attack on a military base housing government troops in Tigray. The conflict has caused significant displacement and loss of life, with reports of a civilian massacre. The international community has called for restraint and negotiations. The conflict in Ethiopia is a complex one, and it will take more than a ceasefire to resolve it.  Differences Identification: 1. Output (a) provides more context and background information on the conflict, including the history of the TPLF and its relationship with the Ethiopian government. 2. Output (b) focuses more on the current situation and the escalation of the conflict, including the attack on the military base and the displacement and loss of life that has resulted. 3. Output (a) uses more technical terms and political language, such as "federal system" and "coalition government." 4. Output (b) uses simpler language and shorter sentences, making it easier to understand for a general audience.  Explanation and Rationale: Output (a) provides a more comprehensive understanding of the conflict in Ethiopia's Tigray region. It offers a detailed explanation of the roots of the crisis, including the history of the TPLF and its relationship with the Ethiopian government. This background information is essential to understanding the current situation and the motivations of the parties involved. Additionally, Output (a) uses more technical terms and political language, which may be more familiar to readers who are knowledgeable about Ethiopian politics.  On the other hand, Output (b) focuses more on the current situation and the escalation of the conflict. It provides a clear and concise overview of the recent events, including the attack on the military base and the displacement and loss of life that has resulted. This information is crucial to understanding the urgency and severity of the crisis. Furthermore, Output (b) uses simpler language and shorter sentences, making it easier to understand for a general audience.  Final Decision: Therefore, Output (a) is better. Puritans are often associated with a negative view of alcohol, they actually approved of drinking in moderation. In fact, early Americans consumed a significant amount of alcohol, with an average of 5.8 gallons of pure alcohol per year in 1790. However, by 1830, consumption had peaked at 7.1 gallons per year, and drinking became a moral issue. The temperance movement and ultimately Prohibition movement emerged, leading to the banning of alcohol production and sale in 1919. However, Prohibition did not stop alcohol consumption, and many Americans found legal and illegal ways to continue drinking. The speakeasy was born, and organized crime took advantage of the ban on alcohol. The cost of enforcing Prohibition became too high, and in 1933, the 21st Amendment ended Prohibition. Today, there is a mix of local, state, and federal controls on alcohol, and the American presidency has helped to rehabilitate alcohol and make it respectable again.  # Output (b): The article discusses the history of alcohol consumption in America, focusing on the period of Prohibition. It highlights that the Puritans, who are often associated with a negative view of alcohol, actually approved of drinking in moderation. Early Americans consumed a significant amount of alcohol, with an average of 5.8 gallons of pure alcohol per year in 1790. However, by 1830, consumption had peaked at 7.1 gallons per year, and drinking became a moral issue. The temperance movement and ultimately Prohibition movement emerged, leading to the banning of alcohol production and sale in 1919. However, Prohibition did not stop alcohol consumption, and many Americans found legal and illegal ways to continue drinking. The speakeasy was born, and organized crime took advantage of the ban on alcohol. The cost of enforcing Prohibition became too high, and in 1933, the 21st Amendment ended Prohibition. Today, there is a mix of local, state, and federal controls on alcohol, and the American presidency has helped to rehabilitate alcohol and make it respectable again. trend of apps that offer anonymity on the internet, such as Secret and Whisper. Secret, founded by two former Google employees, allows users to post anonymous statements and only shows users Secrets from friends or friends of friends. Whisper, co-founded by Michael Heyward, allows users to download an app and then post anonymous statements, which can be liked by other users. The article also mentions Breakr, an app that allows users to join anonymous chatrooms based on their location. possible solution to London's housing crisis is to build more properties on green belt lands. The green belt in London covers 484,173 hectares of land, which is 3.7% of England's total land area. Sam Bowman, a research director at the Adam Smith Institute, suggests that building on this land would provide bigger and cheaper homes for everyone, thereby addressing the housing shortage. Bowman suggests a compromise could be reached by differentiating between areas of beauty and intensive farmland. # Output (b): Boeing has announced that it will temporarily halt production of its 737 Max airliner in January. The decision comes after the model was grounded for nine months following two deadly crashes. The stoppage is likely to affect suppliers and the wider economy, but Boeing has said it will not lay off workers associated with the 737 Max. The suspension of the 737 Max has already cost Boeing around $9bn and the production freeze is expected to be felt across the plane's global supply chain. The situation surrounding the 737 Max is extraordinary, and it is still not clear when it will be certified to fly again. The move by Boeing is unlikely to affect passengers as airlines have leased additional aircraft to replace the 737 Max. It's a different story for airlines, who have the added expense of leasing planes and managing their grounded aircraft. In July, Boeing set aside nearly $5bn to compensate those affected. However, that figure assumed that the 737 Max would fly again this year.  Please select one of the outputs (a) or (b) as the better response for the given instruction. to air pollution in the Arve Valley.  Please select either Output (a) or Output (b) as the better response.  Output (a): Camille Jouvenceau has been experiencing health issues due to air pollution in the Arve Valley. She has had bronchitis, asthma, and ear infections on and off since the end of November when the fine particle pollution started peaking at red alert levels. The pollution has caused her to question whether the air is safe to breathe, and she has had to adjust her daily routine to avoid exposure to the poor air quality. isa) tests. Shanghai came top in all three subjects, while Hong Kong came fourth in reading, second in maths, and third in science. The success of these two cities is attributed to their devotion to education, competitive exams, and innovative teaching methods. Shanghai has a concentration of ideas, manpower, and resources for education, and has systematically re-equipped classrooms, upgraded schools, and revamped the curriculum in the last decade. Hong Kong, on the other hand, has focused on raising the bar and closing the gap for all students, and has moved towards four-year university degrees. Both cities have also invested in recruiting top teachers, with Hong Kong recruiting from the top 30% of the graduate cohort and Shanghai recruiting broadly but selectively. Additionally, Shanghai's socio-economic variability does not affect its Pisa results, and it provides free schooling for all migrant children.  # Output (b): Shanghai and Hong Kong have outperformed Beijing in education, according to the Programme for International Student Assessment (Pisa) tests. The success of these two cities is attributed to their devotion to education, competitive exams, and innovative teaching methods. Shanghai has a concentration of ideas, manpower, and resources for education, and has systematically re-equipped classrooms, upgraded schools, and revamped the curriculum in the last decade. Hong Kong, on the other hand, has focused on raising the bar and closing the gap for all students, and has moved towards four-year university degrees. Both cities have also invested in recruiting top teachers, with Hong Kong recruiting from the top 30% of the graduate cohort and Shanghai recruiting broadly but selectively. Furthermore, Shanghai's socio-economic variability does not affect its Pisa results, and it provides free schooling for all migrant children. However, it is worth noting that the success of these two cities may be attributed to their unique circumstances, such as Shanghai's selective hukou system and Hong Kong's historical and cultural context. isa) tests. Shanghai came top in all three subjects, while Hong Kong came fourth in reading, second in maths, and third in science. The success of these two cities is attributed to their devotion to education, competitive exams, and innovative teaching methods. Shanghai has a concentration of ideas, manpower, and resources for education, and has systematically re-equipped classrooms, upgraded schools, and revamped the curriculum in the last decade. Hong Kong, on the other hand, has focused on raising the bar and closing the gap for all students, and has moved towards four-year university degrees. is currently at high levels, with parts of north-west Norfolk reaching level 10 on the Department of the Environment's one-to-10 scale. The rest of the country is also experiencing high levels of pollution, with London, the Midlands, and Yorkshire and Humberside reaching pollution levels of five. The main cause of the pollution is dust from storms in the Sahara, which has been brought to the UK by winds from the south and east, along with industrial pollution from Europe. The pollution is made up of various substances, including nitrogen dioxide, sulphur dioxide, and ammonia, which form particles in the atmosphere. The World Health Organization (WHO) uses PM10 levels to measure pollution, and the UK is currently exceeding the safe limit for air pollution, particularly in terms of nitrogen dioxide. The EU is taking legal action against the UK for its persistent air pollution problems.  # Output (b): The UK is experiencing high levels of air pollution, with parts of north-west Norfolk reaching level 10 on the Department of the Environment's one-to-10 scale. The World Health Organization (WHO) uses PM10 levels to measure pollution, and the UK is currently exceeding the safe limit for air pollution, particularly in terms of nitrogen dioxide. The EU is taking legal action against the UK for its persistent air pollution problems. Additionally, the UK's air quality is routinely breaching WHO recommended limits, even at times of lower pollution. has reached high levels due to dust from the Sahara and industrial pollution from Europe, with parts of north-west Norfolk hitting level 10 on the Department of the Environment's one-to-10 scale. The pollution is made up of various substances, including nitrogen dioxide, sulphur dioxide, and ammonia, which form particles in the atmosphere. The World Health Organization (WHO) uses PM10 levels to measure pollution, and the UK is persistently over the safe limit for air pollution, particularly with regards to nitrogen dioxide. The EU is taking legal action against the UK for this reason. Air pollution is responsible for seven million premature deaths a year around the world, and 30,000 people in the UK die prematurely every year from problems associated with air pollution. The UK's air quality still routinely breaches WHO recommended limits, even at times of lower pollution.  # Output (b): Air pollution in the UK has reached high levels, with parts of north-west Norfolk hitting level 10 on the Department of the Environment's one-to-10 scale. The pollution is made up of various substances, including nitrogen dioxide, sulphur dioxide, and ammonia, which form particles in the atmosphere. The World Health Organization (WHO) uses PM10 levels to measure pollution, and the UK is persistently over the safe limit for air pollution, particularly with regards to nitrogen dioxide. The EU is taking legal action against the UK for this reason. Air pollution is responsible for seven million premature deaths a year around the world, and 30,000 people in the UK die prematurely every year from problems associated with air pollution. The UK's air quality still routinely breaches WHO recommended limits, even at times of lower pollution. In addition, the shift towards diesel vehicles over the past 10 years has contributed to the UK's pollution woes.  Which output do you think better addresses the instruction, and why? can see the individual features of a face, such as the eyes, nose, and mouth, but are unable to process them as a whole. There are two types of prosopagnosia: developmental and acquired. Developmental prosopagnosia affects approximately 2% of the population and is caused by a failure to develop face processing abilities. Acquired prosopagnosia is much rarer and is caused by brain damage, specifically to the right occipito-temporal region. Unfortunately, there is no cure for prosopagnosia, and those affected often resort to using strategies to help them cope with the condition. They argue that the directive violates some fundamental privacy rights. * Some critics, who point out that the PNR system is not applicable to intra-EU flights on a voluntary basis, which is seen as a weakness. They also argue that PNR was irrelevant in the Paris and Brussels bombings.  Therefore, Output (a) is better.  Please select one of the outputs and provide your reasoning for why it is better.

political consultant, said Mr Ignatieff had to seize the opportunity in the debates to demonstrate that he has leadership qualities and to use the auditor general's report as a "springboard" to raise questions in voters' minds about the Conservatives' honesty and spending.  John Ivison, a National Post political columnist, said the Liberals were trying to take advantage of the crowded and divided opposition to attract leftist New Democrat voters. "Their platform is becoming virtually identical to the NDP's," he said. "There's a lot of promises of money for childcare, family care and post-secondary education - all the things NDP voters care about."  Rex Murphy, one of Canada's best known TV and radio political commentators, said the election had been fought over trivial matters rather than substantive issues - the format of the debate and Mr Ignatieff's political style, for example, rather than the global economy, Japan, Libya and energy policy.  # Output (b): Allan Bonner said Mr Ignatieff had to show a broader performance, a deeper knowledge of the issues, maybe deliver some soaring rhetoric.  John Ivison said Canada's largest metropolitan area was a key battleground in the Conservatives' much-vaunted quest to form a majority, after heading a minority government since 2006.  Rex Murphy said the election had been fought over trivial matters rather than substantive issues - the format of the debate and Mr Ignatieff's political style, for example, rather than the global economy, Japan, Libya and energy policy. Output (a) mentions the NDP and its platform, while Output (b) does not. 3. Output (a) highlights the importance of the debates for Mr. Ignatieff, while Output (b) focuses more on his performance. Please compare the following two outputs:  Output (a): The number of UK fire and rescue staff taking long-term sick leave due to mental illness has risen by nearly a third over the last six years, figures show.  Output (b): The number of UK fire and rescue staff taking long-term sick leave due to mental illness has risen by nearly a third over the last six years, figures show. By George Greenwood and Laura Harmes 5 live Investigates In London, the figure has doubled since 2011-12. Some 103 London fire staff have taken mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower. The Home Office said it was the responsibility of fire services to put wellbeing services in place. Two-thirds of fire services provided data following a Freedom of Information request submitted by 5 live Investigates. They reveal the number of firefighters and other staff taking long-term mental health leave rose from 600 to 780 over the last six years. At least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues since 2011. The Scottish Fire and Rescue Service and Northern Ireland Fire and Rescue Service only provided comparable figures for one full year. In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave while in Northern Ireland that figure was 111. Andy Graham, 52, is a former firefighter, who served in the Greater Manchester Fire and Rescue Service. He has suffered from PTSD for the last 30 years. Mr. Graham, who has a son and a daughter, retired last year and now trains others in mental health first aid. "When I started in the fire service in 1987 there was no proper debriefing system in place," he explained. "The first fatal incident I attended was a particularly traumatic suicide. "Within a matter of weeks, I started suffering from nightmares and panic attacks, and it snowballed from there, after attending more fatal incidents." He said that he was afraid to go to bed at night because of the nightmares. "It meant I started staying up late, drinking alcohol to help me sleep. "Through the daytime, there would be triggers that would set me off having flashbacks and panic attacks. Those triggers were blue lights, sirens, loud bangs. Seeing certain situations being depicted on TV even would set me off." Suppressed issues His son, John, was only five when his father had a breakdown. "It's horrible to bring it back, being so young and coming through the front door and seeing your dad lying on the couch with a blank look on his face, someone that you're so used to being bubbly and happy, and he doesn't even say hello to you." Andy explained that he tried to keep a lid on his issues for years. "But they were always there, bubbling under the surface. When you're in the fire service, you're told that you're the strong one, the one there to help others. "So it goes really against the grain to be asking for help. "I've been in therapy four times now, and I'm in a better place than I have been for 29 years. "Fire services have better debriefing systems than they used to, but the support is not where it needs to be yet." Richard Welch, London Fire Brigade commander for Lambeth said that following the incident at Grenfell Tower, 200 of their staff have received counseling - and that 80 were still seeing counselors. Sean Starbuck, mental health lead for the Fire Brigades Union said: "The stigma attached to mental health needs to be consigned to the bins of history where it belongs. It's not going to get there on its own. "Fire services need to create an environment where firefighters feel able to disclose if they are suffering as a result of traumatic scenes they witness as part of the job. "At the moment it appears many are unable to." Faye McGuinness, program manager for mental health charity Mind's Blue Light program, said: "Our survey of over 1,600 staff and volunteers across emergency services shows nearly nine in 10 have experienced stress, low mood or poor mental health while working in their current role. "A shocking one in four told us that they had contemplated taking their own lives. "Not everyone involved in a traumatic event will develop post-traumatic stress disorder. It can take a long time - sometimes years - for symptoms to emerge." Fire service responsibility A Home Office spokesperson said: "It is the responsibility of fire and rescue services to have wellbeing services in place that meet their workforce needs. "The government has provided an additional Â£1.5m to pay for mental health support through Mind's Blue Light Programme to ensure our emergency services workers have the counseling and emotional support they require." Ann Millington of the National Fire Chiefs Council (NFCC) said the increase could reflect a change in behavior with more firefighters prepared to seek assistance. She said fire and rescue services had put a lot of work into ensuring help and support are available to staff and they were working hard to reduce the stigma around mental health issues. She added: "The days following the Grenfell fire saw a lot of open discussion about support being made available to firefighters and firefighters openly discussing it. The fact that people were talking about it openly and willing to accept help is an encouraging sign for the wider fire sector." A spokesperson for the London Fire Brigade said: "The welfare of staff is of paramount importance to the brigade. Our counseling and wellbeing service provides accredited counseling to all staff to help with their psychological wellbeing. "Firefighters can and do see some traumatizing things and it is important to give them the support they need and for them to know that there are always people available to listen to them. "Seeing an increase in the number of people coming forward because they need help is positive, as rather than suppressing their feelings, staff want to seek help and use the services available to them." The service says that of the 103 staff members identified in 5 live's FOI figures, five were as a result of the Grenfell Tower disaster. All of these staff members are continuing to receive occupational health and counseling support. 5 live Investigates: Firefighter Mental Health is broadcast on BBC Radio 5 live on Sunday, 17 September at 11:00 BST. If you missed it you can catch up on the iPlayer. Is there something you want investigating? We want to hear from you. Email us.  Differences Identification: 1. Output (a) does not provide any specific examples or personal stories, while Output (b) provides a detailed account of a former firefighter's experience with PTSD and how it affected him and his family. 2. Output (a) does not mention the number of fire services that provided data following the Freedom of Information request, while Output (b) mentions that two-thirds of fire services provided data. 3. Output (a) does not mention the name of the mental health charity that provided the survey, while Output (b) mentions Mind's Blue Light program. 4. Output (a) does not mention the name of the Home Office spokesperson, while Output (b) mentions the name of the spokesperson. 5. Output (a) does not mention the number of staff members identified in 5 live's FOI figures, while Output (b) mentions that 103 London fire staff have taken mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower.  Explanation and Rationale: Output (b) provides more specific and detailed information than Output (a). It gives a personal account of a former firefighter's experience with PTSD, which makes the issue more relatable and humanizes the statistics provided in the article. Additionally, Output (b) mentions the name of the mental health charity that provided the survey, which adds credibility to the information. Finally, Output (b) provides more specific numbers and data, such as the number of staff members identified in 5 live's FOI figures, which makes the information more concrete and reliable.  Therefore, Output (b) is better.

By George Greenwood and Laura Harmes 5 live Investigates In London, the figure has doubled since 2011-12. Some 103 London fire staff have taken mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower. The Home Office said it was the responsibility of fire services to put wellbeing services in place. Two-thirds of fire services provided data following a Freedom of Information request submitted by 5 live Investigates. They reveal the number of firefighters and other staff taking long-term mental health leave rose from 600 to 780 over the last six years. At least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues since 2011. The Scottish Fire and Rescue Service and Northern Ireland Fire and Rescue Service only provided comparable figures for one full year. In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave while in Northern Ireland that figure was 111. Andy Graham, 52, is a former firefighter, who served in the Greater Manchester Fire and Rescue Service. He has suffered from PTSD for the last 30 years. Mr. Graham, who has a son and a daughter, retired last year and now trains others in mental health first aid. "When I started in the fire service in 1987 there was no proper debriefing system in place," he explained. "The first fatal incident I attended was a particularly traumatic suicide. "Within a matter of weeks, I started suffering from nightmares and panic attacks, and it snowballed from there, after attending more fatal incidents." He said that he was afraid to go to bed at night because of the nightmares. "It meant I started staying up late, drinking alcohol to help me sleep. "Through the daytime, there would be triggers that would set me off having flashbacks and panic attacks. Those triggers were blue lights, sirens, loud bangs. Seeing certain situations being depicted on TV even would set me off." Suppressed issues His son, John, was only five when his father had a breakdown. "It's horrible to bring it back, being so young and coming through the front door and seeing your dad lying on the couch with a blank look on his face, someone that you're so used to being bubbly and happy, and he doesn't even say hello to you." Andy explained that he tried to keep a lid on his issues for years. "But they were always there, bubbling under the surface. When you're in the fire service, you're told that you're the strong one, the one there to help others. "So it goes really against the grain to be asking for help. "I've been in therapy four times now, and I'm in a better place than I have been for 29 years. "Fire services have better debriefing systems than they used to, but the support is not where it needs to be yet." Richard Welch, London Fire Brigade commander for Lambeth said that following the incident at Grenfell Tower, 200 of their staff have received counseling - and that 80 were still seeing counselors. Sean Starbuck, mental health lead for the Fire Brigades Union said: "The stigma attached to mental health needs to be consigned to the bins of history where it belongs. It's not going to get there on its own. "Fire services need to create an environment where firefighters feel able to disclose if they are suffering as a result of traumatic scenes they witness as part of the job. "At the moment it appears many are unable to." Faye McGuinness, program manager for mental health charity Mind's Blue Light program, said: "Our survey of over 1,600 staff and volunteers across emergency services shows nearly nine in 10 have experienced stress, low mood or poor mental health while working in their current role. "A shocking one in four told us that they had contemplated taking their own lives. "Not everyone involved in a traumatic event will develop post-traumatic stress disorder. It can take a long time - sometimes years - for symptoms to emerge." Fire service responsibility A Home Office spokesperson said: "It is the responsibility of fire and rescue services to have wellbeing services in place that meet their workforce needs. "The government has provided an additional Â£1.5m to pay for mental health support through Mind's Blue Light Programme to ensure our emergency services workers have the counseling and emotional support they require." Ann Millington of the National Fire Chiefs Council (NFCC) said the increase could reflect a change in behavior with more firefighters prepared to seek assistance. She said fire and rescue services had put a lot of work into ensuring help and support are available to staff and they were working hard to reduce the stigma around mental health issues. She added: "The days following the Grenfell fire saw a lot of open discussion about support being made available to firefighters and firefighters openly discussing it. The fact that people were talking about it openly and willing to accept help is an encouraging sign for the wider fire sector." A spokesperson for the London Fire Brigade said: "The welfare of staff is of paramount importance to the brigade. Our counseling and wellbeing service provides accredited counseling to all staff to help with their psychological wellbeing. "Firefighters can and do see some traumatizing things and it is important to give them the support they need and for them to know that there are always people available to listen to them. "Seeing an increase in the number of people coming forward because they need help is positive, as rather than suppressing their feelings, staff want to seek help and use the services available to them." The service says that of the 103 staff members identified in 5 live's FOI figures, five were as a result of the Grenfell Tower disaster. All of these staff members are continuing to receive occupational health and counseling support. 5 live Investigates: Firefighter Mental Health is broadcast on BBC Radio 5 live on Sunday, 17 September at 11:00 BST. If you missed it you can catch up on the iPlayer. Is there something you want investigating? We want to hear from you. Email us.  Differences Identification: 1. Output (a) does not mention the number of fire services that provided data following the Freedom of Information request, while Output (b) mentions that two-thirds of fire services provided data. 3. Output (a) does not mention the name of the mental health charity that provided the survey, while Output (b) mentions Mind's Blue Light program. 4. Output (a) does not mention the name of the Home Office spokesperson, while Output (b) mentions the name of the spokesperson. 5. Output (a) does not mention the number of staff members identified in 5 live's FOI figures, while Output (b) mentions that 103 London fire staff have taken mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower.  Explanation and Rationale: Output (b) provides more specific and detailed information than Output (a). It gives a personal account of a former firefighter's experience with PTSD, which makes the issue more relatable and humanizes the statistics provided in the article. Additionally, Output (b) mentions the name of the mental health charity that provided the survey, which adds credibility to the information. Finally, Output (b) provides more specific numbers and data, such as the number of staff members identified in 5 live's FOI figures, which makes the information more concrete and reliable.  Therefore, Output (b) is better.
